{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01HpHJV1ztoF9S3f3TiYmQUq","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"BINGO! I found it!\n\nLook at lines 30-44 in nfs3proc.c:\n\n```c\nstatic int\nnfs3_rpc_wrapper(struct rpc_clnt *clnt, struct rpc_message *msg, int flags)\n{\n\tint res;\n\tdo {\n\t\tres = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n\t\tif (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n\t\t\tbreak;\n\t\tfreezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n\t\tres = -ERESTARTSYS;\n\t} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n\treturn res;\n}\n\n#define rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags)\tnfs3_rpc_wrapper(clnt, msg, flags)\n```\n\nThe problem is:1. rpc_call_sync is called2. If res == -EJUKEBOX, it sleeps with freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe3. Then it sets res = -ERESTARTSYS\n4. Then it loops and calls rpc_call_sync again5. The loop continues while fatal_signal_pending(current) is FALSE6. When the loop exits (because fatal_signal_pending(current) is TRUE or res != -EJUKEBOX and break happens), it returns res\n\nNow, the issue is: the function returns -ERESTARTSYS even when the underlying RPC call succeeded! This happens if:1. The first rpc_call_sync returns -EJUKEBOX2. The sleep is interrupted by a fatal signal3. fatal_signal_pending(current) becomes TRUE\n4. The loop exits\n5. res is still -ERESTARTSYS\n6. This value is returned\n\nSo the bug is in the nfs3_rpc_wrapper function! When the sleep is interrupted by a fatal signal, it sets res = -ERESTARTSYS and exits the loop, BUT it should return the actual status of the last rpc_call_sync, not the error status.\n\n\nLet me trace through the loop more carefully. The do-while executes rpc_call_sync, checks if the result isn't -EJUKEBOX to break early, otherwise sleeps and sets res to -ERESTARTSYS before checking the signal condition. The core issue is that when a fatal signal arrives during the sleep, the loop terminates with res still holding -ERESTARTSYS rather than attempting another call or returning the actual RPC result. fatal signal pending, the loop exits with res = -ERESTARTSYS. But the actual RPC call might have already completed successfully in the background, and the client is ignoring that successful response. The issue becomes clearer when looking at the bug report—tcpdump shows the server replied without error, yet the client returns -ERESTARTSYS instead. This suggests the wrapper is abandoning a valid server response when a signal arrives during the retry logic.\n\nThe regression from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 is a key clue. The nfs3_rpc_wrapper function with this specific retry behavior must have been introduced or significantly changed between those versions, which would explain why this bug didn't exist {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01C1gUEiMHUBm3jCQVpdHV68","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"## Summary\n\nI've successfully localized the NFS mount disappearance bug to the **`nfs3_rpc_wrapper` function in `fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c`** (lines 30-44).\n\n### Root Cause Analysis\n\n**The Bug:** The `nfs3_rpc_wrapper` function has a critical flaw in its JUKEBOX error retry logic:\n\n1. When the NFS server responds with a `JUKEBOX` error (indicating a temporary server-side delay), the wrapper enters a retry loop\n2. It calls `freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe()` to sleep and retry\n3. **After the sleep, it unconditionally sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS`**\n4. If a fatal signal arrives during this sleep (which happens during autofs mount expiration/unmount), the while loop condition `!fatal_signal_pending(current)` becomes false\n5. The function returns **-ERESTARTSYS (-512) without retrying the RPC call**, even though the server may have already sent a valid reply\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug:**\n- The getattr RPC call fails with error -512\n- This causes `nfs_revalidate_inode()` to fail (as seen in kernel logs)\n- `nfs_lookup_revalidate()` marks the `/storage` dentry as invalid\n- The `/storage` autofs mount is unmounted, along with all submounts\n\n**Why It's a Regression (3.14.12 → 4.1.15):**\nThe issue occurs specifically during autofs mount expiration when the kernel sends signals to tasks waiting on the NFS mount to trigger unmount cleanup.
